	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" >Paul Allen</h1>
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		<div id="contentSub2"></div>
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other people named Paul Allen, see <a href="/wiki/Paul_Allen_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Paul Allen (disambiguation)">Paul Allen (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">American businessman, investor and philanthropist (1953-2018)</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt"> 
 
</p>
<table class="infobox biography vcard" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold"><div class="fn" style="display:inline">Paul </div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Relatives</th><td><a href="/wiki/Jody_Allen" title="Jody Allen">Jody Allen</a> (sister)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Website</th><td><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.paulallen.com/">www<wbr />.paulallen<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Paul Gardner Allen</b> (January 21, 1953 – October 15, 2018) was an American <a href="/wiki/Business_magnate" title="Business magnate">business magnate</a>, computer programmer, researcher, investor, and philanthropist. He was best known for co-founding <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft Corporation</a> with childhood friend <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a> in 1975, which helped spark the <a href="/wiki/Microcomputer_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Microcomputer revolution">microcomputer revolution</a> of the 1970s and 1980s, later making Microsoft the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">personal computer</a> software company.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Allen was ranked as the <a href="/wiki/The_World%27s_Billionaires" title="The World&#39;s Billionaires">44th-wealthiest person in the world</a> by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> in 2018, with an estimated net worth of $20.3 billion at the time of his death.<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes400_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes400-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Allen left active operations at Microsoft in early 1983 after a <a href="/wiki/Hodgkin_lymphoma" title="Hodgkin lymphoma">Hodgkin lymphoma</a> diagnosis, remaining on its board as vice chairman. He and his sister, <a href="/wiki/Jody_Allen" title="Jody Allen">Jody Allen</a>, founded <a href="/wiki/Vulcan_Inc." title="Vulcan Inc.">Vulcan Inc.</a> in 1986,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> a privately held company that managed his various business and philanthropic efforts. He had a multi-billion dollar investment portfolio including technology and media companies, scientific research, real estate holdings, private space flight ventures, and stakes in other sectors. He owned the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Seahawks" title="Seattle Seahawks">Seattle Seahawks</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a><sup id="cite_ref-seahawks_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seahawks-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Portland_Trail_Blazers" title="Portland Trail Blazers">Portland Trail Blazers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-trailblazers_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trailblazers-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and was part-owner of the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Sounders_FC" title="Seattle Sounders FC">Seattle Sounders FC</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-soccer_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soccer-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In 2000 he resigned from his position on Microsoft's board and assumed the post of senior strategy advisor to the company's management team.
</p><p>Allen was also the founder of the Allen Institutes for <a href="/wiki/Allen_Institute_for_Brain_Science" title="Allen Institute for Brain Science">Brain Science</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Allen_Institute_for_Artificial_Intelligence" class="mw-redirect" title="Allen Institute for Artificial Intelligence">Artificial Intelligence</a><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Allen_Institute_for_Cell_Science" title="Allen Institute for Cell Science">Cell Science</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> as well as companies like <a href="/wiki/Stratolaunch_Systems" title="Stratolaunch Systems">Stratolaunch Systems</a><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Apex_Learning" title="Apex Learning">Apex Learning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> He gave more than $2&#160;billion to causes such as education, wildlife and environmental conservation, the arts, healthcare, community services and more.<sup id="cite_ref-Expanded_bio_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Expanded_bio-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, he funded the first manned private <a href="/wiki/Spaceplane" title="Spaceplane">spaceplane</a> with <a href="/wiki/SpaceShipOne" title="SpaceShipOne">SpaceShipOne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Collier_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collier-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Airandspace.si.edu_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airandspace.si.edu-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> He received numerous awards and honors in several different professions and was listed among the <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100"><i>Time</i> 100 Most Influential People in the World</a> in 2007 and 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-TIME_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TIME-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Allen was diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Non-Hodgkin_lymphoma" title="Non-Hodgkin lymphoma">Non-Hodgkin lymphoma</a> in 2009. He died of <a href="/wiki/Septic_shock" title="Septic shock">septic shock</a> related to the cancer on October 15, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-Inquisitr_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inquisitr-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg/220px-Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg/330px-Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg/440px-Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="811" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Allen (left) with <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a> at <a href="/wiki/Lakeside_School_(Seattle)" title="Lakeside School (Seattle)">Lakeside School</a> in 1970</div></div></div>
<p>Allen was born on January 21, 1953, in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, Washington, to Kenneth Sam Allen and Edna Faye (née Gardner) Allen.<sup id="cite_ref-more_than_money_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-more_than_money-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> He attended <a href="/wiki/Lakeside_School_(Seattle,_Washington)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lakeside School (Seattle, Washington)">Lakeside School</a>, a private school in Seattle where he befriended <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a>, with whom he shared an enthusiasm for computers, and they used Lakeside's <a href="/wiki/Teletype_Corporation" title="Teletype Corporation">Teletype</a> terminal to develop their programming skills on several time-sharing computer systems.<sup id="cite_ref-before_microsoft_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-before_microsoft-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> They also used the laboratory of the Computer Science Department of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington" title="University of Washington">University of Washington</a>, doing personal research and computer programming; they were banned from the laboratory in 1971 for abuse of their privileges there.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gates and Allen joined with <a href="/wiki/Ric_Weiland" title="Ric Weiland">Ric Weiland</a> and Gates' childhood best friend and first collaborator, Kent Evans, to form the Lakeside Programming Club and find bugs in <a href="/wiki/Computer_Center_Corporation" title="Computer Center Corporation">Computer Center Corporation</a>'s software, in exchange for extra computer time. In 1972, after Evans' sudden death due to a mountain climbing accident, Gates turned to Allen for help finishing an automated system of Lakeside's entire class scheduling procedure.<sup id="cite_ref-leibovich20001231_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leibovich20001231-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> They then formed <a href="/wiki/Traf-O-Data" title="Traf-O-Data">Traf-O-Data</a> to make traffic counters based on the <a href="/wiki/Intel_8008" title="Intel 8008">Intel 8008</a> processor. According to Allen, he and Gates would go "dumpster diving" in their teenage years for computer program code.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Allen attained a perfect <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> score of 1600<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and went to <a href="/wiki/Washington_State_University" title="Washington State University">Washington State University</a>, where he joined the <a href="/wiki/Phi_Kappa_Theta" title="Phi Kappa Theta">Phi Kappa Theta</a> fraternity.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> He dropped out of college after two years to work as a programmer for <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a> in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> near <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> where Gates was enrolled.<sup id="cite_ref-before_microsoft_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-before_microsoft-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Allen convinced Gates to drop out of Harvard in order to create <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-abc2007_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc2007-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Microsoft">Microsoft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Microsoft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:197px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Altair_Basic_Sign.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Altair_Basic_Sign.jpg/195px-Altair_Basic_Sign.jpg" decoding="async" width="195" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Altair_Basic_Sign.jpg/293px-Altair_Basic_Sign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Altair_Basic_Sign.jpg/390px-Altair_Basic_Sign.jpg 2x" data-file-width="954" data-file-height="1275" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Altair_Basic_Sign.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The title page of the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_language" title="Assembly language">assembly language</a> code that produced <a href="/wiki/Altair_BASIC" title="Altair BASIC">Altair BASIC</a>, developed by Allen, Gates, and <a href="/wiki/Monte_Davidoff" title="Monte Davidoff">Monte Davidoff</a>, with two early Microsoft business cards showing Gates as president and Allen as vice president</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Microsoft" title="History of Microsoft">History of Microsoft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft#1972–1985:_Founding" title="Microsoft">Microsoft §&#160;1972–1985: Founding</a></div>
<p>Allen and Gates formed Microsoft in 1975 in <a href="/wiki/Albuquerque,_New_Mexico" title="Albuquerque, New Mexico">Albuquerque, New Mexico</a>, and began marketing a <a href="/wiki/BASIC" title="BASIC">BASIC</a> programming language interpreter, with their first employee being high school friend and collaborator <a href="/wiki/Ric_Weiland" title="Ric Weiland">Ric Weiland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thocp1_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thocp1-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-before_microsoft_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-before_microsoft-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Allen came up with the name of "Micro-Soft", a combination of "microcomputer" and "software".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Microsoft committed to delivering a disk operating system (<a href="/wiki/DOS" title="DOS">DOS</a>) to IBM for the original <a href="/wiki/IBM_PC" class="mw-redirect" title="IBM PC">IBM PC</a> in 1980, although they had not yet developed one, and Allen spearheaded a deal for Microsoft to purchase <a href="/wiki/86-DOS" title="86-DOS">QDOS</a> (Quick and Dirty Operating System) written by <a href="/wiki/Tim_Paterson" title="Tim Paterson">Tim Paterson</a> who was employed at <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Computer_Products" title="Seattle Computer Products">Seattle Computer Products</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> As a result of this transaction, Microsoft secured a contract to supply the DOS that ran on IBM's PC line, which opened the door to Allen's and Gates' wealth and success.<sup id="cite_ref-before_microsoft_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-before_microsoft-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The relationship between Allen and Gates became strained as they argued even over small things.<sup id="cite_ref-leibovich20001231_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leibovich20001231-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Allen effectively left Microsoft in 1982 after being diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Hodgkin%27s_lymphoma" class="mw-redirect" title="Hodgkin&#39;s lymphoma">Hodgkin's lymphoma</a>, though he remained on the board of directors as vice chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-before_microsoft_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-before_microsoft-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fortune2018_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune2018-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Gates reportedly asked Allen to give him some of his shares to compensate for the higher amount of work that Gates was doing.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> According to Allen,  Gates said that he "did almost everything on <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_BASIC" title="Microsoft BASIC">BASIC</a>" and the company should be split 60–40 in his favor. Allen agreed to this arrangement, which Gates later renegotiated to 64–36.<sup id="cite_ref-cnet2013_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnet2013-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In 1983, Gates tried to buy Allen out at $5 per share, but Allen refused and left the company with his shares intact; this made him a billionaire when Microsoft went public.<sup id="cite_ref-cnet2013_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnet2013-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Gates later repaired his relationship with Allen, and the two men donated $2.2 million to their childhood school Lakeside in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-leibovich20001231_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leibovich20001231-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> They remained friends for the rest of Allen's life.<sup id="cite_ref-Gates_Mourns_Allen_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gates_Mourns_Allen-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Allen resigned from his position on the Microsoft board of directors on November 9, 2000, but he remained as a senior strategy advisor to the company's executives.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In January 2014, he still held 100 million shares of Microsoft.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Businesses_and_investments">Businesses and investments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Businesses and investments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Vulcan_Inc." title="Vulcan Inc.">Vulcan Inc.</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_and_technology">Financial and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Financial and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><b>Vulcan Capital</b> is an investment arm of Allen's Seattle-based Vulcan Inc., which has managed his personal fortune. In 2013, Allen opened a new Vulcan Capital office in <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California" title="Palo Alto, California">Palo Alto, California</a>, to focus on making new investments in emerging technology and internet companies.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Patents:</b> Allen held 43 patents from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Patent_and_Trademark_Office" title="United States Patent and Trademark Office">United States Patent and Trademark Office</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Apps:</b> Allen backed A.R.O., the startup behind the mobile app Saga;<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> SportStream, a social app for sports fans;<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and a content-management app called <a href="/wiki/Fayve" title="Fayve">Fayve</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Interval Research Corporation:</b> In 1992, Allen and <a href="/wiki/David_Liddle" title="David Liddle">David Liddle</a> co-founded <a href="/wiki/Interval_Research_Corporation" title="Interval Research Corporation">Interval Research Corporation</a>, a Silicon Valley-based laboratory and new business incubator that was dissolved in 2000 after generating over 300 patents,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> four of which were the subject of Allen's August 2010 <a href="/wiki/Patent_infringement" title="Patent infringement">patent infringement</a> lawsuit against <a href="/wiki/AOL" title="AOL">AOL</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>, <a href="/wiki/EBay" title="EBay">eBay</a>, Facebook, Google, <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Office_Depot" class="mw-redirect" title="Office Depot">Office Depot</a>, <a href="/wiki/OfficeMax" title="OfficeMax">OfficeMax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Staples_Inc." title="Staples Inc.">Staples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a>, and YouTube.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wsj2010_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj2010-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Ticketmaster:</b> In November 1993, Allen invested more than $325 million to acquire 80% of <a href="/wiki/Ticketmaster" title="Ticketmaster">Ticketmaster</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20yrs_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20yrs-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, <a href="/wiki/Home_Shopping_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Home Shopping Network">Home Shopping Network</a> acquired 47.5% of Allen's stock in exchange for $209 million worth of their own stock.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Charter Communications:</b> In 1998, Allen bought a controlling interest in <a href="/wiki/Charter_Communications" title="Charter Communications">Charter Communications</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Charter filed for bankruptcy reorganization in 2009, with Allen's loss estimated at $7 billion. Allen kept a small stake after Charter emerged from reorganization, worth $535 million in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The company's 2016 purchase and subsequent merger of <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner_Cable" title="Time Warner Cable">Time Warner Cable</a> with Charter's subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/Spectrum_(cable_service)" class="mw-redirect" title="Spectrum (cable service)">Spectrum</a>, made Charter Communications the second-largest cable company in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aerospace">Aerospace</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Aerospace">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Allen confirmed that he was the sole investor behind aerospace engineer and entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Burt_Rutan" title="Burt Rutan">Burt Rutan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/SpaceShipOne" title="SpaceShipOne">SpaceShipOne</a> <a href="/wiki/Suborbital" class="mw-redirect" title="Suborbital">suborbital</a> commercial <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">spacecraft</a> on October 4, 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The craft was developed and flown by <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Aerospace_Ventures" title="Mojave Aerospace Ventures">Mojave Aerospace Ventures</a>, which was a joint venture between Allen and Rutan's aviation company, <a href="/wiki/Scaled_Composites" title="Scaled Composites">Scaled Composites</a>. SpaceShipOne climbed to an altitude of 377,591 feet (115,090&#160;m) over the <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Air_and_Space_Port" title="Mojave Air and Space Port">Mojave Air and Space Port</a> and was the first privately funded effort to successfully put a civilian in suborbital space. It won the <a href="/wiki/Ansari_X_Prize" title="Ansari X Prize">Ansari X Prize</a> competition and received the $10&#160;million prize.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 13, 2011, Allen announced the creation of <a href="/wiki/Stratolaunch_Systems" title="Stratolaunch Systems">Stratolaunch Systems</a>, based at the <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Air_and_Space_Port" title="Mojave Air and Space Port">Mojave Air and Space Port</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Scaled_Composites_Stratolaunch" title="Scaled Composites Stratolaunch">Stratolaunch</a> is a proposed orbital launch system consisting of a dual-bodied, 6-engine jet aircraft, capable of carrying a rocket to high altitude; the rocket would then separate from its carrier aircraft and fire its own engines to complete its climb into orbit. If successful, this project would be the first wholly privately funded space transport system.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Stratolaunch, which is partnering with <a href="/wiki/Orbital_ATK" class="mw-redirect" title="Orbital ATK">Orbital ATK</a> and Scaled Composites, is intended to launch in inclement weather, fly without worrying about the availability of launch pads and to operate from different locations. Stratolaunch plans to ultimately host six to ten missions per year.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> On April 13, 2015, Vulcan Aerospace was announced. It is the company within Allen's Vulcan Inc. that plans and executes projects to shift how the world conceptualizes space travel through cost reduction and on-demand access.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 13, 2019, the Stratolaunch aircraft made its maiden flight, reaching 15,000&#160;ft (4,600&#160;m) and 165&#160;kn (305&#160;km/h) in a 2 h 29 min flight.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>  Stratolaunch CEO Jean Floyd offered this comment: "We dedicate this day to the man who inspired us all to strive for ways to empower the world's problem-solvers, Paul Allen. Without a doubt, he would have been exceptionally proud to see his aircraft take flight".<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of the end of May 2019, Stratolaunch Systems Corporation is closing operations.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 208.66666666667px"><div style="width: 208.66666666667px">
