		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 189.33333333333px"><div style="width: 189.33333333333px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 187.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:-0.16666666666666px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:SpaceShipOne.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/SpaceShipOne.jpg/281px-SpaceShipOne.jpg" decoding="async" width="188" height="126" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/SpaceShipOne.jpg/422px-SpaceShipOne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/SpaceShipOne.jpg/563px-SpaceShipOne.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>SpaceShipOne at the <a href="/wiki/National_Air_and_Space_Museum" title="National Air and Space Museum">National Air and Space Museum</a>
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Real_estate">Real estate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Real estate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Allen's <b>Vulcan Real Estate</b><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> division offers development and portfolio management services, and is known for the redevelopment of the <a href="/wiki/South_Lake_Union,_Seattle" title="South Lake Union, Seattle">South Lake Union</a> neighborhood immediately north of downtown Seattle.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Vulcan has developed 6.3&#160;million square feet (590,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of new residential, office, retail and <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> research space, and has a total development capacity of 10,000,000&#160;sq&#160;ft (930,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>). Vulcan advocated for the Seattle Streetcar line known as <a href="/wiki/South_Lake_Union_Streetcar" title="South Lake Union Streetcar">South Lake Union Streetcar</a>, which runs from Seattle's <a href="/wiki/Westlake_Center" title="Westlake Center">Westlake Center</a> to the south end of Lake Union.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> called Allen's South Lake Union investment "unexpectedly lucrative" and one that led to his firm selling a 1,800,000-square-foot (170,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) office complex to <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon.com</a> for US$1.16&#160;billion, one of the most expensive office deals ever in Seattle.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> "It's exceeded my expectations", Allen said of the South Lake Union development.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues">Venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><b>Sports and event centers</b>: Allen funded the development of Portland's <a href="/wiki/Moda_Center" title="Moda Center">Moda Center</a>, which he purchased in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> He also contributed $130&#160;million to help build <a href="/wiki/CenturyLink_Field" class="mw-redirect" title="CenturyLink Field">CenturyLink Field</a> in Seattle.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Seattle_Cinerama" title="Seattle Cinerama">Seattle Cinerama</a>:</b> Allen purchased Seattle's historic Cinerama Theater in 1998, and upgraded it with 3-D capability and digital sound, in addition to interior and exterior refurbishing. The theater installed the world's first commercial digital laser projector in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/The_Hospital_Club" title="The Hospital Club">Hospital Club</a>:</b> Allen opened the Hospital Club in London in 2004 as a professional and social hub for people working in the creative arts.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>  A second location in Los Angeles is under construction.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_team_ownership">Sports team ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Sports team ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Portland_Trail_Blazers">Portland Trail Blazers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Portland Trail Blazers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Portland_Trail_Blazers" title="Portland Trail Blazers">Portland Trail Blazers</a></div>
<p>Allen purchased the Portland Trail Blazers NBA team in 1988 from California real estate developer <a href="/wiki/Larry_Weinberg_(businessman)" class="mw-redirect" title="Larry Weinberg (businessman)">Larry Weinberg</a> for $70&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-trailblazers_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trailblazers-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> He was instrumental in the development and funding of the <a href="/wiki/Moda_Center" title="Moda Center">Moda Center</a> (previously known as the Rose Garden), the arena where the Blazers play. He purchased the arena on April 2, 2007, and stated that this was a major milestone and a positive step for the franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-before_microsoft_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-before_microsoft-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-quiet_owner_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quiet_owner-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The Allen-owned Trail Blazers reached the playoffs 19 times including the <a href="/wiki/NBA_Finals" title="NBA Finals">NBA Finals</a> in 1990 and 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> According to <i>Forbes</i>, the Blazers were valued at $940&#160;million in 2015 and ranked No. 12 out of 30 NBA teams.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Seattle_Seahawks">Seattle Seahawks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Seattle Seahawks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Seahawks" title="Seattle Seahawks">Seattle Seahawks</a></div>
<p>Allen purchased the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL's</a> <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Seahawks" title="Seattle Seahawks">Seattle Seahawks</a> in <a href="/wiki/1997_Seattle_Seahawks_season" title="1997 Seattle Seahawks season">1997</a> from owner <a href="/wiki/Ken_Behring" title="Ken Behring">Ken Behring</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-astdl_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-astdl-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-comsspu_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comsspu-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> who had attempted to move the team to <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">southern California</a> the <a href="/wiki/1996_Seattle_Seahawks_season" title="1996 Seattle Seahawks season">previous year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-seahawks_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seahawks-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bvows_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bvows-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bdwart_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bdwart-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Herman Sarkowsky, a former Seahawks minority owner, told <i><a href="/wiki/The_Seattle_Times" title="The Seattle Times">The Seattle Times</a></i> about Allen's decision to buy the team, "I'm not sure anybody else in this community would have done what [Allen] did."<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In 2002, the team moved into <a href="/wiki/CenturyLink_Field" class="mw-redirect" title="CenturyLink Field">CenturyLink Field</a>, after Allen invested into the upgrade of the stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Acquired for <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>200&#160;million in 1997,<sup id="cite_ref-astdl_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-astdl-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-comsspu_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comsspu-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> the Seahawks were valued at $1.33&#160;billion in August 2014 by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i>, which says the team has "one of the most rabid fan bases in the NFL".<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Under the helm of Allen, the Seahawks made the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> three times following <a href="/wiki/NFC_Championship_Game" title="NFC Championship Game">NFC Championship</a> victories (<a href="/wiki/2005_Seattle_Seahawks_season" title="2005 Seattle Seahawks season">2005</a>, <a href="/wiki/2013_Seattle_Seahawks_season" title="2013 Seattle Seahawks season">2013</a>, <a href="/wiki/2014_Seattle_Seahawks_season" title="2014 Seattle Seahawks season">2014</a>), and won <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVIII" title="Super Bowl XLVIII">Super Bowl XLVIII</a> in February 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Seattle_Sounders_FC">Seattle Sounders FC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Seattle Sounders FC">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Sounders_FC" title="Seattle Sounders FC">Seattle Sounders FC</a></div>
<p>Allen's Vulcan Sports &amp; Entertainment is part of the ownership team of the Seattle Sounders FC, a <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a> (MLS) franchise that began play in 2009 at <a href="/wiki/CenturyLink_Field" class="mw-redirect" title="CenturyLink Field">CenturyLink Field</a>, a stadium which was also controlled by Allen.<sup id="cite_ref-soccer_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soccer-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The ownership team also includes film producer <a href="/wiki/Joe_Roth" title="Joe Roth">Joe Roth</a>, businessman <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Hanauer" title="Adrian Hanauer">Adrian Hanauer</a>, and comedian <a href="/wiki/Drew_Carey" title="Drew Carey">Drew Carey</a>. The Sounders sold out every home game during its first season, setting a new MLS record for average match attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Filmmaking">Filmmaking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Filmmaking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Allen and his sister, <a href="/wiki/Jody_Allen" title="Jody Allen">Jody Allen</a>, together were the owners and executive producers of <a href="/wiki/Vulcan_Productions" title="Vulcan Productions">Vulcan Productions</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> a television and film production company headquartered in Seattle within the entertainment division of Vulcan Inc. Their films have received various recognition, ranging from a <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Award" title="Peabody Award">Peabody Award</a><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> to <a href="/wiki/Independent_Spirit_Awards" title="Independent Spirit Awards">Independent Spirit Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-vulcanproductions.com_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vulcanproductions.com-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Grammy" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy">Grammys</a><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Emmys" class="mw-redirect" title="Emmys">Emmys</a>.
</p><p>In 2014 alone, Allen's film, <i>We The Economy,</i> won 12&#160;awards including a <a href="/wiki/Webby_award" class="mw-redirect" title="Webby award">Webby award</a> for best Online News &amp; Politics Series. The films have also been nominated for <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globes" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globes">Golden Globes</a><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a><sup id="cite_ref-vulcanproductions.com_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vulcanproductions.com-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> among many others. Vulcan Productions' films and documentary projects include <i><a href="/wiki/Far_from_Heaven" title="Far from Heaven">Far from Heaven</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-vulcanproductions.com_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vulcanproductions.com-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> (2002), <i><a href="/wiki/Hard_Candy_(film)" title="Hard Candy (film)">Hard Candy</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> (2005), <i>Rx for Survival: A Global Health Challenge</i><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> (2005), <i><a href="/wiki/Where_God_Left_His_Shoes" title="Where God Left His Shoes">Where God Left His Shoes</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> (2006), <i><a href="/wiki/Judgment_Day:_Intelligent_Design_on_Trial" title="Judgment Day: Intelligent Design on Trial">Judgment Day: Intelligent Design on Trial</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> (2007), <i>This Emotional Life</i><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> (2010), <i>We The Economy</i><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> (2014) <i><a href="/wiki/Racing_Extinction" title="Racing Extinction">Racing Extinction</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> (2015) and Oscar-nominated <i><a href="/wiki/Body_Team_12" title="Body Team 12">Body Team 12</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> (2015).
</p><p>In 2013, Vulcan Productions co-produced the Richard E. Robbins-directed film <i><a href="/wiki/Girl_Rising_(film)" title="Girl Rising (film)">Girl Rising</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> which tells the stories of girls from different parts of the world who seek an education. Globally, over 205&#160;million households watched <i>Girl Rising</i> during the CNN premier,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> and over 4&#160;million people have engaged with <i>Girl Rising</i> through websites and social media. Through the associated 10×10 program, over $2.1&#160;million has been donated to help girls receive an education worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Also in 2013, Vulcan Productions signed on as a producing partner of <i><a href="/wiki/Pandora%27s_Promise" title="Pandora&#39;s Promise">Pandora's Promise</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> a documentary about nuclear power, directed by Oscar-nominated director <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stone_(director)" title="Robert Stone (director)">Robert Stone</a>. It was released on CNN in November 2013. A variety of college and private screenings as well as panel discussions have been hosted throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Philanthropy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Allen gave more than $2&#160;billion towards the advancement of science, technology, education, wildlife conservation, the arts, and community services in his lifetime.<sup id="cite_ref-Expanded_bio_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Expanded_bio-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The Paul G. Allen Family Foundation, which he founded with his sister <a href="/wiki/Jody_Allen" title="Jody Allen">Jody Allen</a>, was established to administer a portion of Allen's philanthropic contributions. Since its formation, the foundation has given more than $494&#160;million to over 1,500 nonprofits; and,<sup id="cite_ref-pgafamilyfoundation.org_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pgafamilyfoundation.org-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> in 2010, Allen became a signatory of <a href="/wiki/The_Giving_Pledge" title="The Giving Pledge">The Giving Pledge</a>, promising to give at least half of his fortune to philanthropic causes.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Allen received commendations for his philanthropic commitments including the <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie_Medal_of_Philanthropy" class="mw-redirect" title="Andrew Carnegie Medal of Philanthropy">Andrew Carnegie Medal of Philanthropy</a><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> and <i>Inside Philanthropy'</i>s "Philanthropist of the Year".<sup id="cite_ref-insidephilanthropy.com_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidephilanthropy.com-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_research">Science and research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Science and research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_G._Allen_at_Allen_Institute_for_Brain_Science.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Paul_G._Allen_at_Allen_Institute_for_Brain_Science.jpg/220px-Paul_G._Allen_at_Allen_Institute_for_Brain_Science.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Paul_G._Allen_at_Allen_Institute_for_Brain_Science.jpg/330px-Paul_G._Allen_at_Allen_Institute_for_Brain_Science.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Paul_G._Allen_at_Allen_Institute_for_Brain_Science.jpg/440px-Paul_G._Allen_at_Allen_Institute_for_Brain_Science.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1054" data-file-height="792" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_G._Allen_at_Allen_Institute_for_Brain_Science.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Allen (right) studies a brain sample with Allan Jones, CEO of the <a href="/wiki/Allen_Institute_for_Brain_Science" title="Allen Institute for Brain Science">Allen Institute for Brain Science</a>, in 2011</div></div></div>
<p>In September 2003, Allen launched the <a href="/wiki/Allen_Institute_for_Brain_Science" title="Allen Institute for Brain Science">Allen Institute for Brain Science</a> with a $100&#160;million contribution dedicated to understanding how the human brain works. In total, Allen donated $500&#160;million to the institute, making it his single largest philanthropic recipient. Since its launch, the Allen Institute for Brain Science has taken a Big Science and Open Science approach to tackle projects. The institute makes research tools available to the scientific community using an open data model.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Some of the institute's most notable projects include the Allen Mouse Brain Atlas, Allen Human Brain Atlas and the Allen Mouse Brain Connectivity Atlas. The Allen Institute is also helping to advance and shape the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>'s <a href="/wiki/BRAIN_Initiative" title="BRAIN Initiative">BRAIN Initiative</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Human_Brain_Project" title="Human Brain Project">Human Brain Project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Founded in 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Allen_Institute_for_Artificial_Intelligence" class="mw-redirect" title="Allen Institute for Artificial Intelligence">Allen Institute for Artificial Intelligence</a> (AI2)'s main focus is to research and engineer <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The Institute is modeled after the <a href="/wiki/Allen_Institute_for_Brain_Science" title="Allen Institute for Brain Science">Allen Institute for Brain Science</a> and led by researcher and professor, Dr. <a href="/wiki/Oren_Etzioni" title="Oren Etzioni">Oren Etzioni</a>. AI2 has undertaken four main projects, Aristo, <a href="/wiki/Semantic_Scholar" title="Semantic Scholar">Semantic Scholar</a>, Euclid, and Plato. Project Aristo is working to build an AI system capable of passing an 8th-grade science exam.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2014, Allen committed $100&#160;million to create the <a href="/wiki/Allen_Institute_for_Cell_Science" title="Allen Institute for Cell Science">Allen Institute for Cell Science</a> in Seattle. The institute is investigating and creating a virtual model of cells in the hope of bringing forth treatment of different diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Like the institutes before it, all data generated and tools developed will be made publicly available online.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Launched in 2016 with a $100&#160;million commitment, The <a href="/wiki/Paul_G._Allen_Frontiers_Group" title="Paul G. Allen Frontiers Group">Paul G. Allen Frontiers Group</a> aims to discover and support ideas at the frontier of bioscience in an effort to accelerate the pace of discovery.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The group will target scientists and research areas that "some might consider out-of-the-box at the very edges of knowledge".<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Allen launched the Allen Distinguished Investigators Awards (ADI) in 2010 to support scientists pursuing early-stage research projects who often have difficulty securing funding from traditional sources.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Allen donated the seed money to build <a href="/wiki/SETI" class="mw-redirect" title="SETI">SETI</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Allen_Telescope_Array" title="Allen Telescope Array">Allen Telescope Array</a>, eventually contributing $30&#160;million to the project.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Paul_Allen%27s_flower_fly" title="Paul Allen&#39;s flower fly">Paul Allen's flower fly</a> was named in recognition of his contributions to <a href="/wiki/Dipterology" class="mw-redirect" title="Dipterology">Dipterology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment_and_conservation">Environment and conservation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Environment and conservation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Allen provided more than $7&#160;million to fund a census of elephant populations in Africa, the largest such endeavour since the 1970s. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Elephant_Census" title="Great Elephant Census">Great Elephant Census</a> team flew over 20 countries to survey African savannah elephants.  The survey results were published in 2015 and showed rapid rates of decline which were accelerating.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He began supporting the <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia" title="University of British Columbia">University of British Columbia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sea_Around_Us_(organization)" title="Sea Around Us (organization)">Sea Around Us</a> Project in 2014 to improve data on global fisheries as a way to fight illegal fishing. Part of his $2.6&#160;million in funding went towards the creation of FishBase,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> an online database about adult finfish.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Allen funded the Global FinPrint initiative, launched in July 2015, a three-year survey of sharks and rays in coral reef areas. The survey is the largest of its kind and designed to provide data to help conservation programs.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Allen backed <a href="/wiki/Washington_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington state">Washington state</a> initiative 1401 to prohibit the purchase, sale and distribution of products made from 10 endangered species including elephants, rhinos, lions, tigers, leopards, cheetahs, marine turtles, pangolins, sharks and rays. The initiative gained enough signatures to be on the state's ballot on November 3, 2015, and passed.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Alongside the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Transportation" title="United States Department of Transportation">United States Department of Transportation</a> (USDOT), Allen and Vulcan Inc. launched the Smart City Challenge,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> a contest inviting American cities to transform their transportation systems. Created in 2015 with the USDOT's $40&#160;million commitment as well as $10&#160;million from Allen's Vulcan Inc., the challenge aims to create a first-of-its-kind modern city that will demonstrate how cities can improve quality of life while lowering greenhouse gas emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> The winning city was <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus, Ohio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/International_SeaKeepers_Society" title="International SeaKeepers Society">International SeaKeepers Society</a>, Allen hosted its proprietary SeaKeeper 1000TM oceanographic and atmospheric monitoring system on all three of his megayachts.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Allen funded the building of microgrids, which are small-scale power grids that can operate independently, in Kenya, to help promote reusable energy and empower its businesses and residents.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> He was an early investor in the Mawingu Networks, a wireless and solar-powered Internet provider which aims to connect rural Africa with the world, and Off Grid Electric, a company focused on providing solar energy to people in emerging nations.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ebola">Ebola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ebola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2014, Allen pledged at least $100&#160;million toward the fight to end the <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_epidemic_in_West_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebola virus epidemic in West Africa">Ebola virus epidemic in West Africa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> making him the largest private donor in the Ebola crisis. He also created a website called TackleEbola.org<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> as a way to spread awareness and serve as a vehicle for donors to fund projects in need. The site additionally highlighted organizations working to stop Ebola that Allen supported such as <a href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9decins_Sans_Fronti%C3%A8res" title="Médecins Sans Frontières">Médecins Sans Frontières</a>, <a href="/wiki/Partners_in_Health" class="mw-redirect" title="Partners in Health">Partners in Health</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Program_USA" class="mw-redirect" title="World Food Program USA">World Food Program USA</a>. On April 21, 2015, Allen brought together key leaders in the Ebola fight at the Ebola Innovation Summit in San Francisco. The summit aimed to share key learnings and reinforce the need for continued action and support to bring the number of Ebola cases down to zero, which was achieved in January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2015, the Paul G. Allen Family Foundation announced it would award seven new grants totaling $11&#160;million to prevent future widespread outbreaks of the virus.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exploration">Exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2012, along with his research team and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>, Allen attempted to retrieve the bell from <a href="/wiki/HMS_Hood_(51)" class="mw-redirect" title="HMS Hood (51)">HMS&#160;<i>Hood</i></a>, which sank in the <a href="/wiki/Denmark_Strait" title="Denmark Strait">Denmark Strait</a> during World War II, but the attempt failed due to poor weather. On August 7, 2015, they tried again and recovered the bell in very good condition.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> It was restored and put on display in May 2016 in the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_the_Royal_Navy,_Portsmouth" title="National Museum of the Royal Navy, Portsmouth">National Museum of the Royal Navy, Portsmouth</a>, in remembrance of the 1,415 crewmen lost.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2015, Allen funded the research ship <a href="/wiki/RV_Petrel" title="RV Petrel">RV&#160;<i>Petrel</i></a>, and he purchased the ship in 2016. The project team aboard <i>Petrel</i> was responsible for locating the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_battleship_Musashi" title="Japanese battleship Musashi">Japanese battleship&#160;<i>Musashi</i></a> in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, on Allen's directions, <i>Petrel</i> found <a href="/wiki/USS_Indianapolis_(CA-35)" title="USS Indianapolis (CA-35)">USS&#160;<i>Indianapolis</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Ward_(DD-139)" class="mw-redirect" title="USS Ward (DD-139)">USS&#160;<i>Ward</i></a>, the wrecks of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Surigao_Strait" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Surigao Strait">Battle of Surigao Strait</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ormoc_Bay" title="Battle of Ormoc Bay">Battle of Ormoc Bay</a>. In 2018, <i>Petrel</i> found a lost US Navy C-2A Greyhound aircraft in the Philippine Sea, <a href="/wiki/USS_Lexington_(CV-2)" title="USS Lexington (CV-2)">USS&#160;<i>Lexington</i></a> in the Coral Sea and the <a href="/wiki/USS_Juneau_(CL-52)" title="USS Juneau (CL-52)">USS&#160;<i>Juneau</i></a> off the coast of the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_arts">The arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: The arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Allen established several non-profit community institutions that feature his private collections of historic artifacts. These include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Pop_Culture" title="Museum of Pop Culture">Museum of Pop Culture</a>, or MoPOP, is a nonprofit museum, dedicated to contemporary popular culture inside a <a href="/wiki/Frank_Gehry" title="Frank Gehry">Frank Gehry</a>-designed building at <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Center" title="Seattle Center">Seattle Center</a>, established in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Flying_Heritage_Collection" class="mw-redirect" title="Flying Heritage Collection">Flying Heritage Collection</a>, which showcases restored vintage military aircraft and armaments primarily from the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> era, established in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>STARTUP Gallery, a permanent exhibit at the <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_Museum_of_Natural_History_and_Science" title="New Mexico Museum of Natural History and Science">New Mexico Museum of Natural History and Science</a> in <a href="/wiki/Albuquerque" class="mw-redirect" title="Albuquerque">Albuquerque</a> dedicated to the history of the <a href="/wiki/Microcomputer" title="Microcomputer">microcomputer</a>, established in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Living_Computers:_Museum_%2B_Labs" title="Living Computers: Museum + Labs">Living Computer: Museum + Labs</a>, a collection of vintage computers in working order and available for interactive sessions on-site or through networked access, opened to the public in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>An active art collector, Allen gifted more than $100&#160;million to support the arts.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> On October 15, 2012, the Americans for the Arts gave Allen the <a href="/wiki/Eli_Broad" title="Eli Broad">Eli and Edythe Broad</a> Award for Philanthropy in the Arts.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Allen also loaned out more than 300 pieces from his private art collection to 47 different venues. In 2013, Allen sold <a href="/wiki/Barnett_Newman" title="Barnett Newman">Barnett Newman</a>'s <i>Onement VI</i> (1953) at <a href="/wiki/Sotheby%27s" title="Sotheby&#39;s">Sotheby's</a> in New York for $43.8&#160;million which at the time was the record price to have been paid for a work by the abstract artist.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, Allen founded the Seattle Art Fair, a four-day event with 60-plus galleries from around the world including the participation of the <a href="/wiki/Gagosian_Gallery" title="Gagosian Gallery">Gagosian Gallery</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Zwirner" title="David Zwirner">David Zwirner</a>, and many others. The event drew thousands and inspired other satellite fairs throughout the city.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2016, Allen announced the launch of Upstream Music Fest + Summit,<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> an annual festival fashioned after <a href="/wiki/South_by_Southwest" title="South by Southwest">South by Southwest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Held in <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_Square,_Seattle" title="Pioneer Square, Seattle">Pioneer Square</a>, the first festival took place in May 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Allen_and_Steve_Wozniak_at_the_Living_Computer_Museum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Paul_Allen_and_Steve_Wozniak_at_the_Living_Computer_Museum.jpg/220px-Paul_Allen_and_Steve_Wozniak_at_the_Living_Computer_Museum.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Paul_Allen_and_Steve_Wozniak_at_the_Living_Computer_Museum.jpg/330px-Paul_Allen_and_Steve_Wozniak_at_the_Living_Computer_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Paul_Allen_and_Steve_Wozniak_at_the_Living_Computer_Museum.jpg/440px-Paul_Allen_and_Steve_Wozniak_at_the_Living_Computer_Museum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4002" data-file-height="2908" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Allen_and_Steve_Wozniak_at_the_Living_Computer_Museum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Allen and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Wozniak" title="Steve Wozniak">Steve Wozniak</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Living_Computer_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Living Computer Museum">Living Computer Museum</a> in 2017</div></div></div>
<p>In 1989, Allen donated $2&#160;million to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington" title="University of Washington">University of Washington</a> to construct the Allen Library, which was named after his father Kenneth S. Allen, a former associate director of the University of Washington library system.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> In the same year, Allen donated an additional $8&#160;million to establish the Kenneth S. Allen Library Endowment.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, the endowment was renamed the Kenneth S. and Faye G. Allen Library Endowment after Allen's mother (a noted bibliophile) died.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2002, Allen donated $14&#160;million to the University of Washington to construct the Paul G. Allen Center for Computer Science and Engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The building was dedicated in October 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, Allen announced a gift of $26&#160;million to build the Paul G. Allen School of Global Animal Health at <a href="/wiki/Washington_State_University" title="Washington State University">Washington State University</a>, his alma mater. The gift was the largest private donation in the university's history.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, Allen pledged a $10 million donation over four years for the creation of the Allen Discovery Centers at <a href="/wiki/Tufts_University" title="Tufts University">Tufts University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>. The centers would fund research that would read and write the morphogenetic code. Over eight years the donation could be as much as $20 million.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, Allen donated $40 million (with an additional $10 million added by Microsoft) to reorganize the University of Washington's Computer Science and Engineering department into the Paul G. Allen School of Computer Science and Engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>While Allen expressed interest in romantic love and one day having a family,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> he never married and had no children.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> His marriage plans with his first girlfriend were cancelled as he felt he "was not ready to marry at 23".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> He was sometimes considered <a href="/wiki/Recluse" title="Recluse">reclusive</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Allen_and_the_Underthinkers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Paul_Allen_and_the_Underthinkers.jpg/220px-Paul_Allen_and_the_Underthinkers.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Paul_Allen_and_the_Underthinkers.jpg/330px-Paul_Allen_and_the_Underthinkers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Paul_Allen_and_the_Underthinkers.jpg/440px-Paul_Allen_and_the_Underthinkers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Allen_and_the_Underthinkers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Paul Allen and the Underthinkers perform at the Allen Institute for Brain Science's 10th-anniversary gala</div></div></div>
<p>Allen received his first electric guitar at the age of sixteen, and was inspired to play it by listening to <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Jimi Hendrix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> In 2000, Allen played rhythm guitar on the independently produced album <i>Grown Men</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, he had a major label release on Sony's Legacy Recordings; <i>Everywhere at Once</i> by Paul Allen and the Underthinkers.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> PopMatters.com described <i>Everywhere at Once</i> as "a quality release of blues-rock that's enjoyable from start to finish".<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 7, 2018, an interview with <a href="/wiki/Quincy_Jones" title="Quincy Jones">Quincy Jones</a> was released by the magazine <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i> on their <i>Vulture</i> website. In this interview, Jones said that he had extreme respect for <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a>, his band <a href="/wiki/Cream_(band)" title="Cream (band)">Cream</a>, and Allen. Referencing Allen's Hendrix-like play, the article mentioned a jam session on a yacht with <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yachting">Yachting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Yachting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Octopus1_Grand_Cayman_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Octopus1_Grand_Cayman_2010.jpg/220px-Octopus1_Grand_Cayman_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Octopus1_Grand_Cayman_2010.jpg/330px-Octopus1_Grand_Cayman_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Octopus1_Grand_Cayman_2010.jpg/440px-Octopus1_Grand_Cayman_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Octopus1_Grand_Cayman_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Allen's <a href="/wiki/Octopus_(yacht)" title="Octopus (yacht)"><i>Octopus</i></a> off the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a> in 2010</div></div></div>
<p>Allen's 414-foot (126&#160;m) yacht, <a href="/wiki/Octopus_(yacht)" title="Octopus (yacht)"><i>Octopus</i></a>, was launched in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> As of 2019, it was 20th on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_motor_yachts_by_length" title="List of motor yachts by length">list of motor yachts by length</a>. The yacht is equipped with two helicopters, a submarine, an <a href="/wiki/Remotely_operated_underwater_vehicle" title="Remotely operated underwater vehicle">ROV</a>, a swimming pool, a music studio and a basketball court.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> <i>Octopus</i> is a member of <a href="/wiki/AMVER" title="AMVER">AMVER</a>, a voluntary group ship reporting system used worldwide by authorities to arrange assistance for those in distress at sea.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> The ship is also known for its annual celebrity-studded parties which Allen hosted at the <a href="/wiki/Cannes_film_festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Cannes film festival">Cannes film festival</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> where Allen and his band played for guests. These performances included musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_A._Stewart" class="mw-redirect" title="David A. Stewart">David A. Stewart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> <i>Octopus</i> was also used in the search for a missing American pilot and two officers whose plane disappeared off <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> and the study of a rare fish called a <a href="/wiki/Coelacanth" title="Coelacanth">coelacanth</a> among many others.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Allen also owned <a href="/wiki/Tatoosh_(yacht)" title="Tatoosh (yacht)"><i>Tatoosh</i></a>, which is one of the world's 100 largest yachts. In January 2016, it was reported that <i>Tatoosh</i> allegedly damaged coral in the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> In April 2016, the Department of Environment (DoE) and Allen's Vulcan Inc. successfully completed a restoration plan to help speed recovery and protect the future of coral in this area.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Idea_Man"><i>Idea Man</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Idea Man">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2011, Allen's memoir, <i><a href="/wiki/Idea_Man:_A_Memoir_by_the_Cofounder_of_Microsoft" class="mw-redirect" title="Idea Man: A Memoir by the Cofounder of Microsoft">Idea Man: A Memoir by the Cofounder of Microsoft</a></i>, was published by Portfolio, a <a href="/wiki/Penguin_Group" title="Penguin Group">Penguin Group</a> imprint. The book recounts how Allen became enamored with computers at an early age, conceived the idea for Microsoft, recruited his friend Bill Gates to join him, and launched what would become the world's most successful software company. It also explores Allen's business and creative ventures following his 1983 departure from Microsoft, including his involvement in SpaceShipOne, his purchase of the Portland Trail Blazers and Seattle Seahawks, his passion for music, and his ongoing support for scientific research. The book made <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times_Best_Seller_list" title="The New York Times Best Seller list">The New York Times Best Seller list</a></i> and the paperback version, which included a new epilogue, came out on October 30, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Allen was diagnosed with Stage 1-A <a href="/wiki/Hodgkin%27s_lymphoma" class="mw-redirect" title="Hodgkin&#39;s lymphoma">Hodgkin's lymphoma</a> in 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-cnet2013_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnet2013-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Although his cancer was successfully treated by several months of <a href="/wiki/Radiation_therapy" title="Radiation therapy">radiation therapy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-fortune2018_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune2018-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Allen was diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Non-Hodgkin_lymphoma" title="Non-Hodgkin lymphoma">non-Hodgkin lymphoma</a> in 2009. Likewise, the cancer was successfully treated until it returned in 2018, which ultimately caused his death by <a href="/wiki/Septic_shock" title="Septic shock">septic shock</a> on October 15, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Inquisitr_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inquisitr-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> He was 65 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several Seattle-area landmarks, including the <a href="/wiki/Space_Needle" title="Space Needle">Space Needle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Center" title="Columbia Center">Columbia Center</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lumen_Field" title="Lumen Field">Lumen Field</a>, as well as various Microsoft offices throughout the United States, were illuminated in blue on November 3, 2018, as a tribute to Allen.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> He was also honored by his early business partner and lifelong friend <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a>, who said in a statement:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Paul loved life and those around him, and we all cherished him in return. He deserved much more time, but his contributions to the world of technology and philanthropy will live on for generations to come. I will miss him tremendously.<sup id="cite_ref-Gates_Mourns_Allen_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gates_Mourns_Allen-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_recognition">Awards and recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Awards and recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Allen received numerous awards in many different areas, including sports, philanthropy, and the arts:
</p>
<ul><li>In 2004, Allen, <a href="/wiki/Burt_Rutan" title="Burt Rutan">Burt Rutan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doug_Shane" title="Doug Shane">Doug Shane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Melvill" title="Mike Melvill">Mike Melvill</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brian_Binnie" title="Brian Binnie">Brian Binnie</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Collier_Trophy" title="Collier Trophy">Collier Trophy</a> for <a href="/wiki/SpaceShipOne" title="SpaceShipOne">SpaceShipOne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Collier_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collier-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On March 9, 2005, Allen, Rutan, and the rest of the <a href="/wiki/SpaceShipOne" title="SpaceShipOne">SpaceShipOne</a> team were awarded the 2005 <a href="/wiki/National_Air_and_Space_Museum_Trophy" title="National Air and Space Museum Trophy">National Air and Space Museum Trophy</a> for Current Achievement.<sup id="cite_ref-Airandspace.si.edu_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airandspace.si.edu-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2007 and 2008, Allen was listed among the <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100"><i>Time</i> 100 Most Influential People in The World</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TIME_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TIME-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>He received the Vanguard Award from the <a href="/wiki/National_Cable_%26_Telecommunications_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="National Cable &amp; Telecommunications Association">National Cable &amp; Telecommunications Association</a> on May 20, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On October 30, 2008, the Seattle-King County Association of Realtors honored Allen for his "unwavering commitment to nonprofit organizations in the Pacific Northwest and lifetime giving approaching US$1&#160;billion".<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2009, Allen's philanthropy as the long-time owner of the <a href="/wiki/Portland_Trail_Blazers" title="Portland Trail Blazers">Portland Trail Blazers</a> was recognized with an Oregon Sports Award.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On October 26, 2010, Allen was awarded the W. J. S. Krieg Lifetime Achievement Award for his contributions to the field of neuroscience by the Cajal Club.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On January 26, 2011, at Seattle's <a href="/wiki/Benaroya_Hall" title="Benaroya Hall">Benaroya Hall</a>, Allen was named Seattle Sports Commission Sports Citizen of the Year, an award that has been renamed the Paul Allen Award.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2011, Allen was elected to the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On October 15, 2012, Allen received the Eli and Edythe Broad Award for Philanthropy in the Arts at the National Arts Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On February 2, 2014, Allen received a <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_ring" title="Super Bowl ring">Super Bowl ring</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Seahawks" title="Seattle Seahawks">Seattle Seahawks</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Vince_Lombardi_Trophy" title="Vince Lombardi Trophy">Vince Lombardi Trophy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On October 22, 2014, Allen received a Lifetime Achievement Award from <i>Seattle Business</i> magazine for his impact in and around the greater Puget Sound region.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On December 31, 2014, online philanthropy magazine <i>Inside Philanthropy</i> made Allen their inaugural "Philanthropist of the Year"<sup id="cite_ref-insidephilanthropy.com_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidephilanthropy.com-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> for his ongoing effort to stop the Ebola outbreak in West Africa, breaking ground on a new research center in Seattle, and his battle to save the world's oceans.</li>
<li>In 2014, Allen was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="International Space Hall of Fame">International Space Hall of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On July 18, 2015, Ischia Global Film and Music Festival recognized Allen with the Ischia Humanitarian Award. Event organizers honored Allen for his contributions to social issues through his philanthropic efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On August 25, 2015, Allen was named a recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie_Medal_of_Philanthropy" class="mw-redirect" title="Andrew Carnegie Medal of Philanthropy">Andrew Carnegie Medal of Philanthropy</a> for his work to "save endangered species, fight Ebola, research the human brain, support the arts, protect the oceans, and expand educational opportunities for girls".<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On October 3, 2015, the Center for Infectious Disease Research presented Allen with the 2015 "Champion for Global Health Award" for his leadership and effort to fight Ebola.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On December 10, 2016, Allen, as co-owner of the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Sounders" class="mw-redirect" title="Seattle Sounders">Seattle Sounders</a>, won the <a href="/wiki/2016_MLS_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="2016 MLS Cup">2016 MLS Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On October 3, 2019, Allen was posthumously inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Seahawks_Ring_of_Honor" title="Seattle Seahawks Ring of Honor">Seattle Seahawks Ring of Honor</a>, ironically he was the 12th person inducted into the Ring Of Honor, which is a fitting for the number 12, which represents the fans.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honorary_degrees">Honorary degrees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Allen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Honorary degrees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>Honorary degree from the <a href="/wiki/Washington_State_University" title="Washington State University">Washington State University</a>. The university bestowed its highest honor, the Regents' Distinguished Alumnus Award, upon him.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Honorary doctorate in Philosophy from <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela_Metropolitan_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Nelson Mandela Metropolitan University">Nelson Mandela Metropolitan University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Honorary doctorate of Science from the <a href="/wiki/Cold_Spring_Harbor_Laboratory" title="Cold Spring Harbor Laboratory">Cold Spring Harbor Laboratory</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Watson_School_of_Biological_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Watson School of Biological Sciences">Watson School of Biological Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Honorary degree from the <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_Polytechnique_F%C3%A9d%C3%A9rale_de_Lausanne" title="École Polytechnique Fédérale de Lausanne">École Polytechnique Fédérale de Lausanne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>

<li><i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_Silicon_Valley" title="Pirates of Silicon Valley">Pirates of Silicon Valley</a></i>, a 1999 film about the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">personal computer</a>. Allen is portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Josh_Hopkins" title="Josh Hopkins">Josh Hopkins</a>.</li>
